<div id="review_680982552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/680982552" />
    <a title="Crystal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8114559-crystal"><img alt="Crystal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399332166p2/8114559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/680982552?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal" href="/user/show/8114559-crystal">Crystal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680982552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13981616664266355458">I have been ever so impatiently awaiting the last book in the Trust Trilogy, I just could not wait to see what was going to happen to Alistair, Sophia, and yes even Ethan. There were a few more characters that I was curious to see what was going to happen to in Pandora's Box. <br/><br/><br/>WOW, where do I start?<br/><br/><br/>Cristiane Serruya has written a conclusion to this trilogy that not only made me laugh, cry my eyes out at times, but also kept me on the edge of my seat for quite a while. Ms. Serruya has done a fabul</span>
  <span id="freeText13981616664266355458" style="display:none">I have been ever so impatiently awaiting the last book in the Trust Trilogy, I just could not wait to see what was going to happen to Alistair, Sophia, and yes even Ethan. There were a few more characters that I was curious to see what was going to happen to in Pandora's Box. <br /><br /><br />WOW, where do I start?<br /><br /><br />Cristiane Serruya has written a conclusion to this trilogy that not only made me laugh, cry my eyes out at times, but also kept me on the edge of my seat for quite a while. Ms. Serruya has done a fabulous job with this great trilogy. I've loved each one. <br /><br />Once I started reading Pandora's Box I quickly found my deep connection to Sophia once again. Also that precious little girl Gabriella. I also have a fondness for Alistair and only found myself wanting to smack him a time or two in between loving his relationship with Sophia and Gabriella. <br /><br />There is so much that happens in this book I don't want to give anything away. It's just too good for you not to get the chance to experience all the joys, sorrows, and drama for yourself. <br /><br />I will say that there are some very dramatic moments that left me speechless and sitting on the edge of my seat waiting to see how they were going to unfold. Ms. Serruya has a talent for capturing my attention that is for sure. <br /><br />In Pandora's Box a lot of things are answered that I have been wondering about through the other books. I felt a nice conclusion with this book but I also found deep sadness. I won't tell you what made me so unbelievably sad. I will tell you that if you have read the other books in this series you very well may want to grab the box of Kleenex and keep it handy for parts of Pandora's Box. I think you might need it, I know I sure did. <br /><br />There is plenty of steamy scenes between Alistair and Sophia, their relationship really is a strong one, built on love. Sophia has found her love and Alistair has as well. They both need each other to help heal the wounds of the past. Sophia knows she can count on Alistair to be there when she needs him the most and he is. <br /><br />Let me see what more may I tell you about this fabulous story that will not give to much away? I think that even if you have not read the other two books in this trilogy you will enjoy this book. Yes, there is a lot of information in the first two but please don't let the fact you haven't read them yet keep you from grabbing this one now. I think you will enjoy it as a conclusion to the story or as a stand alone. I think this truly is my favorite book in the trilogy. <br /><br />This book is one very well written emotional story, with lots of drama, and some really hot and steamy scenes as well. I found myself quickly turning pages because there were so many things happening I had to find out what in the world could happen next or what new information may be revealed. As you can tell I really did enjoy this story. I can not wait to see what Cristiane Serruya may come up with for us lucky readers next. I know I sure would not hesitate to pick up another book written by her. <br /><br />I was given the wonderful opportunity to read this book so that I may share my thoughts with you. As always it has been my great pleasure to share my thoughts with you on Trust: Pandora's Box.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13981616664266355458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_803549713" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/803549713" />
    <a title="Morexette " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16593687-morexette"><img alt="Morexette " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437185308p2/16593687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/803549713?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morexette " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morexette " href="/user/show/16593687-morexette">Morexette </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer803549713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12893679646120727770"><b>4.5</b><br/><br/>In all honesty, I did not like the conclusion of the Trust Trilogy as much as the previous two books. My justifications are as follows:<br/><br/>1. The first few chapters were promising although when I reached the mid-chapters of the novel, it feels like I've been diverted into another path - into fringes of the story. And as I read further, more and more fork lanes sprouted from previous chapters. Actually, I am glad I've been led back to the focus and main stories of the novel. <br/><br/>2. Somehow, I find Eth</span>
  <span id="freeText12893679646120727770" style="display:none"><b>4.5</b><br><br>In all honesty, I did not like the conclusion of the Trust Trilogy as much as the previous two books. My justifications are as follows:<br><br>1. The first few chapters were promising although when I reached the mid-chapters of the novel, it feels like I've been diverted into another path - into fringes of the story. And as I read further, more and more fork lanes sprouted from previous chapters. Actually, I am glad I've been led back to the focus and main stories of the novel. <br><br>2. Somehow, I find Ethan's situation - especially his resurgence from "his dark room" to accepting and taking the outside world, the reality, in a more friendly and positive manner, important and relevant, and (for me), should have given more portions in the novel. I could have liked the novel with two dimensions unfolding and slowly integrating in the story (Alistair and Sophia's married life and Ethan's situation).<br><br>But I gave the final installment a <b>4.5</b> because...<br><br>1. Although it can be predicted that danger follows everywhere Sophia, at most, is - I get the hints of kidnapping her in return of ransom, or sabotaging her company or her family and friends or both, or even murder. I'm banking on kidnapping and murder though but I was surprised, gladly surprised, of the outcome. Because of course, a woman as intelligent and surrounded with loved ones as Sophia, she has a very high chance not to die (and from that point, I can finally breathe throughout the novel - although her traumas recurred and I feel bad for her but hey, it's Sophia. She's just one of the few fictional heroines who still stood as a sturdy as a bamboo pole on a duration of a Category 5 hurricane, and I really admire that for her). <br><br>2. IT IS VERY RARE TO BALANCE ROMANCE BETWEEN MYSTERY AND THRILL. I MEAN, HOW MANY CONTEMPORARY ROMANCE NOVELS ARE THERE WHO CONTAIN THESE ELEMENTS BALANCED AND PERFECTLY EXECUTED? BRAVO, CRIS. BRAVO! (This element highlighted throughout the book really stunned me.) <br><br>3. Cris surfaced the facts and reality of love - its brilliance and its imperfections. No matter how perfect one is running his/her company, how he/she is accomplished in life, love is love. It and its characteristics are universal. <br><br><br>4. Ethan's death. (BUT WHY HAS HE GOT TO DIE? WHY? WHY? WHY?) Yes, Ethan's been battered both physically and mentally and socially, and (I think) it's just to, you know, kill him? (My fangirl instincts says no) Anyways, he did not die in vain and he died free from his past troubles and he got a chance to see the real world, the world outside his "dark room", in a better and warmer light than before. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/579669.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12893679646120727770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Thank you, Cristiane Serruya, for your beautiful works that give us readers so many emotions and make us dream.</span>

The love story between Alistair and Sophia continues to grow. We are able to understand the complex character of Ethan. Any other questions we've had regarding the first two books are answered. Five Excellent Stars for me!</span>

<div id="review_790800619" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/790800619" />
    <a title="Divya Nambiar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8480687-divya-nambiar"><img alt="Divya Nambiar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364830820p2/8480687.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Divya Nambiar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Divya Nambiar" href="/user/show/8480687-divya-nambiar">Divya Nambiar</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer790800619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17427039630970799112"><i>'The life of the dead is placed in the memory of the living.'</i><br/><br/>This line refuses to leave my mind. the last page has been turned and the tear drops have been shed. I sit thinking about the joy and sorrow of the very lives led by the characters of the book. Suddenly there was a void. Sophia, Alistair, Gabriela, Nathalie, Ethan... it felt as if I was going to leave them all in the confines of the book. That's when I remembered Cristiane Serruya's words-"It was as if when I finished their stories I h</span>
  <span id="freeText17427039630970799112" style="display:none"><i>'The life of the dead is placed in the memory of the living.'</i><br><br>This line refuses to leave my mind. the last page has been turned and the tear drops have been shed. I sit thinking about the joy and sorrow of the very lives led by the characters of the book. Suddenly there was a void. Sophia, Alistair, Gabriela, Nathalie, Ethan... it felt as if I was going to leave them all in the confines of the book. That's when I remembered Cristiane Serruya's words-"It was as if when I finished their stories I had set them free. They are not mine anymore, they belong to the world and I can still be with them whenever I want." Read more about the interview here- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://critiquedontcriticize.blogspot.in/2014/04/without-self-respect-we-detract-from.html">http://critiquedontcriticize.blogspot...</a><br><br>The demons from within each one of them were finally released, but at what cost? Love, as they say it, is all-sacrificing and all-consuming. Or is it? Love can be an obsession that can endanger one's life. <br><br>Heat,passion and a million other expressions and feelings are no doubt described to the finest detail in this final installation of the Trust Trilogy but what I urge you reader, is to reach to the deeper layers of it. The best part about this series is the in-depth exploration of the human psyche by the author. She has played with the thought processes of the characters very intelligently and each character is a winner here- in one or the other way.<br><br>I would always remain indebted to this author for bringing to the notice of the reader, the widely debated but little answered problem of women empowerment - be it at home or at the workplace. <br><br>What I found amazing is the fact that she gives startling details and shocks the reader by pinpointing issues that grapple to be heard all across the world but are silently throttled in ways we might never even notice. <br><br>This is more than a tale of love, sacrifices and devils of the mind. It's a rediscovery of one's own self in ways we would never know that our minds functioned in!<br><br>P.S. For a new reader of Erotica, this would be a high dose. But be bold enough to venture deeper rather than passing scornful and shocked expressions. Few descriptions make one think about the ultimate and 'does-it-really-happen-?' craziness of the human species!<br><br>Other books by the author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6583811.Cristiane_Serruya" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1353691614p2/6583811.jpg" alt="Cristiane Serruya" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> - <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17982897.The_Modern_Man_A_philosophical_divagation_about_the_evil_banality_of_daily_acts" title="The Modern Man A philosophical divagation about the evil banality of daily acts by Cristiane Serruya" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1369730526s/17982897.jpg" alt="The Modern Man A philosophical divagation about the evil banality of daily acts by Cristiane Serruya" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>Review- <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://critiquedontcriticize.blogspot.in/2013/09/the-modern-man-philosophical-divagation.html">http://critiquedontcriticize.blogspot...</a><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16160314.Trust_A_New_Beginning__Trust_Trilogy___1_" title="Trust A New Beginning (Trust Trilogy, #1) by Cristiane Serruya" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1353446926s/16160314.jpg" alt="Trust A New Beginning (Trust Trilogy, #1) by Cristiane Serruya" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> Review-<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://critiquedontcriticize.blogspot.in/2013/09/trust-new-beginning-book-review.html">http://critiquedontcriticize.blogspot...</a> <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17454163.Trust_Betrayed__Trust_Trilogy___2_" title="Trust Betrayed (Trust Trilogy, #2) by Cristiane Serruya" rel="nofollow noopener">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/726443225?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margarida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margarida" href="/user/show/14877802-margarida">Margarida</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer726443225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16334204921279666396">I'm so glad I won the first book on a goodreads giveaway so freaking glad. I fell in love with these characters with the story. I absolutely loved this trilogy and this last book was the perfect conclusion.<br/><br/>Let me tell you that since the beginning of this book I liked Ethan and I was pretty shocked because in the last book he become super creepy and I just did not like him but in this one damn I fell in love with him.He finally realized that he wasn't the one for Sophia she was his best friend an</span>
  <span id="freeText16334204921279666396" style="display:none">I'm so glad I won the first book on a goodreads giveaway so freaking glad. I fell in love with these characters with the story. I absolutely loved this trilogy and this last book was the perfect conclusion.<br /><br />Let me tell you that since the beginning of this book I liked Ethan and I was pretty shocked because in the last book he become super creepy and I just did not like him but in this one damn I fell in love with him.He finally realized that he wasn't the one for Sophia she was his best friend and nothing more. When he went to India with Sophia and her crew I was thinking oh man his he going to do it?! Please do it <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I really wanted him to adopt that kid. It was such a beautiful scene and it left with a goofy smile on my face <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Then there was Barbara and there were moments I thought they were going to end up together but I totally understood why Ethan did what he did. Finally Cristiane broke my heart I just couldn't believe it when I read that scene I just thought <i>no?!</i> And when the truth sink in and I started laughing I know it wasn't I joke but damn I just laughed and laughed and started yelling <i>REALLY?! REALLY?! WHY?!</i> and then obviously tears came. I think I finished this without believing what happened but I understand why she did it.<br /><br />Now Alistair. This dude and his sexy accent! Every time he said <i>nae</i> or <i>aye</i> I totally melted and when he called Sophia all those adorable names *-* I absolutely love him! He's just so alpha male, always trying to protect Sophia but you know she doesn't let him because she's a badass. Alistair is one of those characters that grew so much and now he's so happy and that makes me so happy too. Him and Gabriela ! They're the cutest thing ever!!<br /><br />Sophia is one of those characters that you just like since the beginning because she has such a strong personality and she doesn't take bulls**t from anyone. I love that about her but in this book she did annoy me about but I don't remember why so it probably wasn't important.<br /><br /><b>Alistair+Sophia= AWESOMENESS</b>!!! I love this two together!! I'm always laughing or I'm jealous because they're perfect together *-* I love when Sophia calls him <b>Lord I’m-so-handsome-and-I-know-it</b> or <b>Lord Caveman</b> it's so funny!!!! I loved the ending they had and I knew the problem Alistair had had to be solved!!! I was so so so so HAPPY! :D<br /><br />One of the things that really makes me love this trilogy is that this isn't just about a romance it's about real things that happen in real life.<br /></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/914760338?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Hennessy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Hennessy" href="/user/show/6981944-john-hennessy">John Hennessy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6981944-john-hennessy?shelf=women-s-fiction">women-s-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6981944-john-hennessy?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6981944-john-hennessy?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer914760338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15368351226779640950">A fantastic, breathtaking and enthralling conclusion to an epic series. Full review to come. <br/><br/>Here it is:-<br/><br/>-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br/><br/>"How can I defeat a nightmare?"<br/><br/>How indeed. Cristiane Serruya's TRUST story is one of the best trilogies I have had the pleasure of reading. A hot romance downplays what this really is: An edge of the seat thriller that leaves you gasping, and I do mean literally.<br/><br/>From 'A New Beginning', through 'Betrayed', to finally reac</span>
  <span id="freeText15368351226779640950" style="display:none">A fantastic, breathtaking and enthralling conclusion to an epic series. Full review to come. <br /><br />Here it is:-<br /><br />-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><br />"How can I defeat a nightmare?"<br /><br />How indeed. Cristiane Serruya's TRUST story is one of the best trilogies I have had the pleasure of reading. A hot romance downplays what this really is: An edge of the seat thriller that leaves you gasping, and I do mean literally.<br /><br />From 'A New Beginning', through 'Betrayed', to finally reach and open 'Pandora's Box', it has been an interesting, intriguing, thrilling, and always enthralling ride.<br /><br />If Book One showed us a rather uncertain, but still very strong Sophia, Book Three reveals Sophia to be in even more charge of what she wants. She is an appealing heroine that you will root for. Why? When she is beautiful, rich, and has men seemingly fall at her feet, you wonder why?<br /><br />Because the story, although it features heavily on Sophia, it is not all about her, and through the other characters - Ethan, Alistair, Tavish...so many in fact that it is a supporting cast that you enjoy, along with Sophia's story.<br /><br />This is good characterisation. When Sophia is not in the story, you think it might lag. It does not, and it's all the more enjoyable when she returns.<br /><br />The descriptive tone of this book, just like the other two in the series, is wonderful. I especially enjoyed the references to Scotland, because although I have been all over the world, and indeed, over the border as far as Glasgow, that was for business....I've never truly visited the country. Cristiane makes you feel like you are there.<br /><br />The date and time stamps reinforce the urgency of the story. These books are long, complex, multi-layered. It will take several re-reads to grasp the quality of this work.<br /><br />So when I have done that, I will come back and edit this review.<br /><br />You can see in every line that the author has put her all into giving us an enthralling conclusion to the TRUST tale. She delivers. And because she does, any reference to it would be a major spoiler.<br /><br />So buy the books, and enjoy them. TRUST me when I say that Pandora's Box shouldn't just be opened....you should rip it apart and throw yourself in!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15368351226779640950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12615550896230546181">Find this review and more at <a href='http://www.lustypenguin.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lusty Penguin Reviews!</a><br/><br/>Cristiane Serruya pens a taught romance with pulse-pounding elements of romantic suspense in <em>Trust: Pandora’s Box</em>, the final installment of the Trust trilogy.<br/><br/>Now married, Alistair and Sophia MacCraig are continuing to work on maintaining the solid relationship they forged in the second book. Unfortunately, not only do Alistair and Sophia inadvertently end up hurting each other, but also outsiders are actively trying to destroy their relationship</span>
  <span id="freeText12615550896230546181" style="display:none">Find this review and more at <a href="http://www.lustypenguin.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Lusty Penguin Reviews!</a><br /><br />Cristiane Serruya pens a taught romance with pulse-pounding elements of romantic suspense in <em>Trust: Pandora’s Box</em>, the final installment of the Trust trilogy.<br /><br />Now married, Alistair and Sophia MacCraig are continuing to work on maintaining the solid relationship they forged in the second book. Unfortunately, not only do Alistair and Sophia inadvertently end up hurting each other, but also outsiders are actively trying to destroy their relationship. To their credit, Alistair and Sophia, through meaningful conversations, are able to work through the hurts that they are inflicting on each other. Since Alistair and Sophia have built a measure of trust, they do not succumb to others who try to destroy their relationship, which I loved about them. At the same time, I loved seeing Ethan Ashford, with Sophia’s encouragement, working to become the man he really wants to be. When the actions of our greedy and mysterious antagonists fail, they take drastic action that threatens Sophia’s life. Although Alistair and Ethan do not get along, they manage to put their personal feelings aside to help save Sophia, leading to a dramatic climax in which not everyone survives, and the bad guys get what’s coming to them. After all they have suffered through separately and together, Alistair and Sophia have a beautiful and satisfying happily ever after, which brought a huge smile to my face.<br /><br />As with the first two books in this series, I was drawn into Serruya’s character-driven romance in <em>Trust: Pandora’s Box</em>. A strong and compelling couple along and the wrap-up of all major plot points <em>Trust: Pandora’s Box</em> a captivating and entertaining conclusion to the Trust trilogy.<br /><br /> <br />I received an eBook copy of the book for the purpose of an honest review. I was not compensated for this review, and all conclusions are my own responsibility.</span>

<div id="review_1039833791" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1039833791" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15138024-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354570659p2/15138024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1039833791?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/15138024-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15138024-erin?shelf=exchange-for-review">exchange-for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1039833791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3293622104708356394">The third book in the Trust series definitely didn't disappoint! I am so sad that the series has ended, but I loved this book, as well as the entire series. <br/><br/>After Sophia and Alistair tie the knot, they believe they would live happily ever after, but this is when everything begins to fall apart. Between a custody battle, lies, and secrets that are being leaked out, Sophia and Alistair's relationship is put to the ultimate test. Can their marriage survive?<br/><br/>I have loved Sophia from the very first bo</span>
  <span id="freeText3293622104708356394" style="display:none">The third book in the Trust series definitely didn't disappoint! I am so sad that the series has ended, but I loved this book, as well as the entire series. <br /><br />After Sophia and Alistair tie the knot, they believe they would live happily ever after, but this is when everything begins to fall apart. Between a custody battle, lies, and secrets that are being leaked out, Sophia and Alistair's relationship is put to the ultimate test. Can their marriage survive?<br /><br />I have loved Sophia from the very first book. She is a very strong and independent woman who is focused on her career and her family. She puts other people's needs and wants before her own, as you can clearly see in this final book. Both Sophia, Alistair, and Ethan are fighting their past demons, ones that could eat them alive, quite literally. Alistair has never been able to fully open up about his feelings, and what has happened in his past. You really begin to see him strive to begin communicating this to Sophia. Alistair is also dealing with his bouts of jealousy, but you see him, with the help of his brother, slowly begin to control some of these stray emotions. Ethan is questioning his love for Sophia, and dealing with his own demons. He works to try to gain peace with his wrongdoings, and his past struggles.<br /><br />I loved the conclusion to the series. I felt that the book tied up very well, and didn't leave any hanging questions. This book has the reader experience many different emotions throughout the book. I loved the ups and downs of it, and I feel the author pulled it together really well. I loved seeing Sophia, Alistair, and Ethan all fighting their own past demons to try to come to terms with their past, and learn to live in the future. I really enjoyed this entire series, and I really hope Cristiane decides to write another series!<br /><br />I was given this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3293622104708356394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14216351774966964572">Trust (Pandora’s Box) Cristiane Serruya<br/><br/>What can I say? Another action packed, thrill ride with many of my favorite characters comes to a satisfying conclusion. Throughout the trilogy, I’ve seen them stumble, grow, break a little, heal a little and love with all their hearts and arts. No spoilers here but the finale provides full satisfaction. There are all the things I craved to read in the first 2 books, especially the excotic locals, the aggravating (but very human) inner turmoil and flaws tha</span>
  <span id="freeText14216351774966964572" style="display:none">Trust (Pandora’s Box) Cristiane Serruya<br /><br />What can I say? Another action packed, thrill ride with many of my favorite characters comes to a satisfying conclusion. Throughout the trilogy, I’ve seen them stumble, grow, break a little, heal a little and love with all their hearts and arts. No spoilers here but the finale provides full satisfaction. There are all the things I craved to read in the first 2 books, especially the excotic locals, the aggravating (but very human) inner turmoil and flaws that fully expand the depth of each individual. Pandora’s Box is a fine completion to this trilogy and although this is the last of the series, I’m sure I will often wonder “what is next” for Sophia. <br /></span>

Thanks for writing such a great series, I look forward to reading your work in the future.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14506353291948164470">Since I love this series, I'm so sad that I finished reading this book. However, I really enjoyed and am satisfied with the conclusion.<br/><br/>I always found some good quotes in this series, and this one, "Tryst: Pandora's Box" also had some. I'm impressed by the authors sense of words.<br/><br/>In this book, I think Sophia's unstable emotion was depicted realistically and it moved me with sympathy. I was totally into the story and often feel her feelings as if they were mine.<br/><br/>I've already missed Sophia. But I bel</span>
  <span id="freeText14506353291948164470" style="display:none">Since I love this series, I'm so sad that I finished reading this book. However, I really enjoyed and am satisfied with the conclusion.<br /><br />I always found some good quotes in this series, and this one, "Tryst: Pandora's Box" also had some. I'm impressed by the authors sense of words.<br /><br />In this book, I think Sophia's unstable emotion was depicted realistically and it moved me with sympathy. I was totally into the story and often feel her feelings as if they were mine.<br /><br />I've already missed Sophia. But I believe that the author will make me enjoy reading with other attractive characters soon!!</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_6567284'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567284-night-embrace"><img alt="Night Embrace (Dark-Hunter, #2)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1362612024l/6567284._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Gq4lAbtlmSpzPHX8vxKTRh2cpuxXgZrGQ8hPr6s4D/HCNxj1akzt4ysygceXVhapaCj5dEuVqiQ/adqblvIu+g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8aHYY/fhe/xfWtZ5hXeu2gaY95NDnhKBch2XuNE3ZAcpOOWXJsgPNQdUIkKtMys1cyyoC1+KImMOvAKM7P1FDA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
